  I wonder if this function is really needed?
  AFAICS the only thing you ever do with its result is checking whether it `== 0` or not.
  But this question is already answered by `HasTASAssignmentOnNode` just below.
  (Which is more efficient - as it doesn't count until the end).
  
  So it seems you could migrate to using that fn and remove this one?

- **pkg/util/tas/tas_assignment.go:337** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-03-15T10:10:05Z

```diff
+func ExpectedPodsOnNode(psa []kueue.PodSetAssignment, nodeName string) int32 {
+	var expected int32
+	for i := range psa {
+		psa := psa[i]
+		if psa.TopologyAssignment == nil {
+			continue
+		}
+		if !IsLowestLevelHostname(psa.TopologyAssignment.Levels) {
+			continue
+		}
+		for domain := range InternalSeqFrom(psa.TopologyAssignment) {
+			if len(domain.Values) > 0 && domain.Values[len(domain.Values)-1] == nodeName {
+				expected += domain.Count
+			}
+		}
+	}
+	return expected
+}
```

  I feel this function name is misleading.
  The code now looks essentially like this:
  
  > Check `HasTASAssignmentOnNode`. But this may miss some cases.
  > So to catch those, check `listTopologyAssignedPods`.
  
  But "topology assigned" sounds very similar to "TAS assignment".
  While what we really use to "catch missed cases" is Pod's _node selector_.
  
  So maybe rather `listNodeSelectorAssignedPods`?

- **pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go:614** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-03-15T14:33:34Z
```diff
@@ -500,6 +573,54 @@ func (r *nodeReconciler) addUnhealthyNode(ctx context.Context, wl *kueue.Workloa
 	return nil
 }
 
+// getPodsToTerminate returns a list of pending pods that are assigned to the node by topology (but not yet scheduled),
+// and a boolean indicating if there is at least one pod to retain (e.g. any scheduled pod).
+func (r *nodeReconciler) getPodsToTerminate(ctx context.Context, wl *kueue.Workload, nodeName string) ([]*corev1.Pod, bool, error) {
+	hasProgressingPods, err := r.hasProgressingPods(ctx, wl, nodeName)
+	if err != nil {
+		return nil, false, fmt.Errorf("list scheduled pods: %w", err)
+	}
+
+	topologyAssignedPods, err := r.listTopologyAssignedPods(ctx, wl, nodeName)
+	if err != nil {
+		return nil, false, fmt.Errorf("list topology assigned pods: %w", err)
+	}
+
+	var podsToTerminate []*corev1.Pod
+	for _, pod := range topologyAssignedPods {
+		if pod.Status.Phase == corev1.PodPending && !utilpod.HasGate(pod, kueue.TopologySchedulingGate) {
+			podsToTerminate = append(podsToTerminate, pod)
+		}
+	}
+
+	return podsToTerminate, hasProgressingPods, nil
+}
+
+func (r *nodeReconciler) hasProgressingPods(ctx context.Context, wl *kueue.Workload, nodeName string) (bool, error) {
+	sliceName := workloadslicing.SliceName(wl)
+	pods, err := ListPodsForWorkloadSlice(ctx, r.client, wl.Namespace, sliceName, client.MatchingFields{
+		coreindexer.PodNodeNameKey: nodeName,
+	})
+	if err != nil {
+		return false, err
+	}
+	for i := range pods {
+		pod := pods[i]
+		if !pod.DeletionTimestamp.IsZero() || utilpod.IsTerminated(pod) {
+			continue
+		}
+		return true, nil
+	}
+	return false, nil
```

  (Optional - for me it's more readable this way)
  
  ```suggestion
      hasProgressingPods := slices.ContainsFunc(pods, func (pod *corev1.Pod) bool {
        return pod.DeletionTimestamp.IsZero() && !utilpod.IsTerminated(pod)
      })
      return hasProgressingPods, nil
  ```

  This does API `List` under the hood. Is the result cached by the client library?

  So I'm wondering if we're certain that cache will prevent re-fetching on the API level?
  (And if not, should we try to pass the results from here to there?)

```diff
+func (r *nodeReconciler) checkPodsOnNode(ctx context.Context, nodeName string, wl *kueue.Workload, untolerated []corev1.Taint, expectedOnNode int32) (workloadHealthCheck, error) {
+	podsToTerminate, hasProgressingPods, err := r.getPodsToTerminate(ctx, wl, nodeName)
+	if err != nil {
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthUnknown}, fmt.Errorf("failed to get pods to terminate for node %s: %w", nodeName, err)
+	}
+
+	if expectedOnNode == 0 {
+		// This node is not part of the workload's topology assignment. If pods are assigned
+		// here (e.g., late pods with old node selectors), they are stray and must be terminated.
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthy, podsToTerminate: podsToTerminate}, nil
+	}
+
+	if shouldWait(hasProgressingPods, len(untolerated)) {
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthUnknown, podsToTerminate: podsToTerminate}, nil
 	}
-	return workloadHealthy, nil
+
+	return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadUnhealthy, podsToTerminate: podsToTerminate}, nil
 }
 
-// listPodsForWorkload returns pods belonging to a workload.
-func (r *nodeReconciler) listPodsForWorkload(ctx context.Context, wl *kueue.Workload) ([]*corev1.Pod, error) {
-	return ListPodsForWorkloadSlice(ctx, r.client, wl.Namespace, workloadslicing.SliceName(wl))
+// shouldWait encapsulates the logic for deciding if we need to
+// wait for pods to be fully created and assigned before declaring a node failure.
+func shouldWait(hasProgressingPods bool, untoleratedCount int) bool {
+	if untoleratedCount == 0 {
+		return hasProgressingPods
+	}
+
+	return hasProgressingPods && features.Enabled(features.TASReplaceNodeOnPodTermination)
```

  Optional: for me it feels easier to read
  
  ```suggestion
  	return hasProgressingPods && (untoleratedCount == 0 || features.Enabled(features.TASReplaceNodeOnPodTermination))
  ```

- **pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go:87** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-03-15T15:42:40Z
```diff
@@ -73,9 +84,9 @@ const (
 	// and is ready for eviction (e.g. all of its pods on the node have fully terminated).
 	workloadUnhealthy
 
-	// workloadTemporarilyHealthy indicates that the workload will need to be evicted from the node,
+	// workloadHealthUnknown indicates that the workload will need to be evicted from the node,
 	// but is not ready yet (e.g. pods are still terminating, or taints are only temporarily tolerated).
-	workloadTemporarilyHealthy
+	workloadHealthUnknown
```

  This name does not feel to fit the description.
  Basically, "we know we should evict but not now" != "we don't know".
  
  OTOH, I see in the code below that you started to use this case for various `err != nil` cases, so I guess that's why the rename.
  
  I'd propose to consider how "stable" it is in your logic that the error cases fall into the "evict later" bucket. And then:
  - If it's stable -> rename this to `workloadToBeEvictedLater` or so.
  - If it's unstable (i.e. might change) -> have both `workloadHealthUnknown` and `workloadToBeEvictedLater` here. 
    They'll be handled same way for now but it's an implementation detail.
  
  WDYT?

- **pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go:614** by [@j-skiba](https://github.com/j-skiba) — 2026-03-16T08:47:40Z

```diff
+// getPodsToTerminate returns a list of pending pods that are assigned to the node by topology (but not yet scheduled),
+// and a boolean indicating if there is at least one pod to retain (e.g. any scheduled pod).
+func (r *nodeReconciler) getPodsToTerminate(ctx context.Context, wl *kueue.Workload, nodeName string) ([]*corev1.Pod, bool, error) {
+	hasProgressingPods, err := r.hasProgressingPods(ctx, wl, nodeName)
+	if err != nil {
+		return nil, false, fmt.Errorf("list scheduled pods: %w", err)
+	}
+
+	topologyAssignedPods, err := r.listTopologyAssignedPods(ctx, wl, nodeName)
+	if err != nil {
+		return nil, false, fmt.Errorf("list topology assigned pods: %w", err)
+	}
+
+	var podsToTerminate []*corev1.Pod
+	for _, pod := range topologyAssignedPods {
+		if pod.Status.Phase == corev1.PodPending && !utilpod.HasGate(pod, kueue.TopologySchedulingGate) {
+			podsToTerminate = append(podsToTerminate, pod)
+		}
+	}
+
+	return podsToTerminate, hasProgressingPods, nil
+}
+
+func (r *nodeReconciler) hasProgressingPods(ctx context.Context, wl *kueue.Workload, nodeName string) (bool, error) {
+	sliceName := workloadslicing.SliceName(wl)
+	pods, err := ListPodsForWorkloadSlice(ctx, r.client, wl.Namespace, sliceName, client.MatchingFields{
+		coreindexer.PodNodeNameKey: nodeName,
+	})
+	if err != nil {
+		return false, err
+	}
+	for i := range pods {
+		pod := pods[i]
+		if !pod.DeletionTimestamp.IsZero() || utilpod.IsTerminated(pod) {
+			continue
+		}
+		return true, nil
+	}
+	return false, nil
```

  I agree, it looks better - done

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-16T10:43:44Z

- **pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go:639** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-16T10:43:44Z

```diff
@@ -500,6 +599,54 @@ func (r *nodeReconciler) addUnhealthyNode(ctx context.Context, wl *kueue.Workloa
 	return nil
 }
 
+// getPodsToTerminate returns a list of pending pods that are assigned to the node
+// (either scheduled or just assigned via topology), and a boolean indicating
+// if there is at least one pod to retain (e.g. running pod).
+func (r *nodeReconciler) getPodsToTerminate(ctx context.Context, wl *kueue.Workload, nodeName string) ([]*corev1.Pod, bool, error) {
+	sliceName := workloadslicing.SliceName(wl)
+
+	scheduledPods, err := ListPodsForWorkloadSlice(ctx, r.client, wl.Namespace, sliceName, client.MatchingFields{
+		"spec.nodeName": nodeName,
+	})
+	if err != nil {
+		return nil, false, fmt.Errorf("list scheduled pods: %w", err)
+	}
+
+	topologyAssignedPods, err := ListPodsForWorkloadSlice(ctx, r.client, wl.Namespace, sliceName, client.MatchingFields{
+		indexer.PodNodeSelectorHostnameKey: nodeName,
+	})
+	if err != nil {
+		return nil, false, fmt.Errorf("list topology assigned pods: %w", err)
+	}
+	var hasRunningPods bool
+	for _, pod := range scheduledPods {
+		if !pod.DeletionTimestamp.IsZero() || utilpod.IsTerminated(pod) {
+			continue
+		}
+		if pod.Status.Phase == corev1.PodRunning {
+			hasRunningPods = true
+			break
+		}
+	}
+
+	var podsToTerminate []*corev1.Pod
+	for _, pod := range scheduledPods {
+		if !pod.DeletionTimestamp.IsZero() || utilpod.IsTerminated(pod) {
+			continue
+		}
+		if pod.Status.Phase == corev1.PodPending && !utilpod.HasGate(pod, kueue.TopologySchedulingGate) {
+			podsToTerminate = append(podsToTerminate, pod)
+		}
```

  The comment is outdated by now, please resolve

```diff
+			continue
+		}
```

```diff
+// isPodAssignedToNode checks if the pod is assigned to the node, either by being scheduled there
+// (spec.nodeName) or by having a TAS assignment that maps to this node (via nodeSelector).
+func isPodAssignedToNode(pod *corev1.Pod, nodeName string, levels []string) bool {
+	if pod.Spec.NodeName != "" {
+		return pod.Spec.NodeName == nodeName
+	}
+	if !utiltas.IsLowestLevelHostname(levels) {
+		return false
+	}
+	return pod.Spec.NodeSelector[corev1.LabelHostname] == nodeName
+}
+
+func getTopologyAssignmentLevelsForPod(pod *corev1.Pod, wl *kueue.Workload, psaMap map[kueue.PodSetReference]*kueue.PodSetAssignment) []string {
+	psName := kueue.PodSetReference(pod.Labels[constants.PodSetLabel])
+	psa, found := psaMap[psName]
+
+	// Fallback to the first assignment if the label is missing (common for simple/plain Pods)
+	if !found && len(wl.Status.Admission.PodSetAssignments) == 1 {
+		psa = &wl.Status.Admission.PodSetAssignments[0]
+		found = true
+	}
+
+	if found && psa.TopologyAssignment != nil {
+		return psa.TopologyAssignment.Levels
+	}
+
+	return nil
+}
+
+// getPodsAssignedToNode returns a list of pods that are assigned to the node (via spec.nodeName)
+// or are assigned by topology assignment but are not scheduled to the node (e.g. because of a taint).
+// It also returns a boolean indicating if there are any pods assigned to the Workload's topology
+// that are still gated by TopologySchedulingGate (missing nodeSelector).
```

  The comment is outdated by now, please resolve

```diff
+func (r *nodeReconciler) checkPodsOnNode(ctx context.Context, nodeName string, wl *kueue.Workload, untolerated []corev1.Taint, expectedOnNode int32) (workloadHealthCheck, error) {
+	podsAssigned, err := r.getPodsAssignedToNode(ctx, wl, nodeName)
+	if err != nil {
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthUnknown}, fmt.Errorf("failed to get pods assigned to node %s: %w", nodeName, err)
+	}

+

+		// This node is not part of the workload's topology assignment. If pods are assigned
+		// here (e.g., late pods with old node selectors), they are stray and must be terminated.
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthy, podsToTerminate: podsToTerminate}, nil
+	}
+
+	if shouldWait(int32(len(podsAssigned)), expectedOnNode, hasPodsToRetain, len(untolerated)) {
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthUnknown}, nil
+	}
+
+	return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadUnhealthy, podsToTerminate: podsToTerminate}, nil
+}
+
+// shouldWait encapsulates the logic for deciding if we need to
+// wait for pods to be fully created and assigned before declaring a node failure.
```

  Indeed the code has changed.
  So let's look at the current version, [this switch](https://github.com/j-skiba/kueue/blob/298f1f62edc8f2ac39e2f83e70ff6995175d9b8f/pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go#L352-L378).
  Sometimes we call `checkPodsOnNode`, sometimes we don't. 
  When we don't, the resulting `workloadHealthCheck` will have `podsToTerminate` unset (= empty).
  This happens in 3 cases:
  - when the FG `TASReplaceNodeOnPodTermination` is disabled
  - [here](https://github.com/j-skiba/kueue/blob/298f1f62edc8f2ac39e2f83e70ff6995175d9b8f/pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go#L364)
  - [here](https://github.com/j-skiba/kueue/blob/298f1f62edc8f2ac39e2f83e70ff6995175d9b8f/pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go#L377)
  
  I'm trying to understand if all these 3 cases are intended?

```diff
 		if apierrors.IsNotFound(err) {

+			return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthy}, nil
 		}
-		return workloadHealthy, err
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthUnknown}, err
 	}

 	ready := utiltas.IsNodeStatusConditionTrue(node.Status.Conditions, corev1.NodeReady)
-
-	if ready && features.Enabled(features.TASReplaceNodeOnNodeTaints) {

-		untolerated, temporarilyTolerated := classifyNoExecuteTaints(ctx, node.Spec.Taints, workload.PodSetsOnNode(wl, nodeName))

-			}

+		// of the topology assignment (expected == 0), we must always check pods
+		// to catch and fail the stray pod.

+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthy}, nil
+	default:

-		}

 		}
-		return workloadTemporarilyHealthy, nil
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthy}, nil
```

  Yes, that's all intended.
  1. When the fg is disabled we don't wait for the pods do we don't call `checkPodsOnNode`
  2. This is a path when nothing happens when a node is reconciled when a taint appears but the `TASReplaceNodeOnNodeTaints` feature is disabled. Basically it a behavior that would be observed before the feature was implemented
  3. This is reached when a node becomes healthy - a taint is removed or becomes ready

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-17T14:13:29Z

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-17T14:20:16Z

- **pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go:308** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-17T14:20:16Z

```diff
 }
 
+// / listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector returns a map of pods that are assigned to this node via nodeSelector, grouped by workload.
+func (r *nodeReconciler) listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector(ctx context.Context, nodeName string) (map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod, error) {
+	var podList corev1.PodList
+	if err := r.client.List(ctx, &podList, client.MatchingFields{indexer.PodNodeSelectorHostnameKey: nodeName}); err != nil {
+		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to list pods for node selector %s: %w", nodeName, err)
+	}
+
+	return groupPodsByWorkload(podList.Items), nil
+}
+
+func groupPodsByWorkload(pods []corev1.Pod) map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod {
+	nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload := make(map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod)
+	for i := range pods {
+		pod := &pods[i]
+		wlName := coreindexer.IndexPodWorkloadSliceName(pod)
+		if len(wlName) > 0 {
+			key := types.NamespacedName{Name: wlName[0], Namespace: pod.Namespace}
```

  I think this use case we should use the Workload name annotation rather than slice. The SliceName corresponds to the name of the first workload in the chain. I think it is not relevant here as it may not exist any longer..

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-17T14:32:38Z

```diff
+// / listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector returns a map of pods that are assigned to this node via nodeSelector, grouped by workload.
+func (r *nodeReconciler) listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector(ctx context.Context, nodeName string) (map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod, error) {
+	var podList corev1.PodList
+	if err := r.client.List(ctx, &podList, client.MatchingFields{indexer.PodNodeSelectorHostnameKey: nodeName}); err != nil {
+		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to list pods for node selector %s: %w", nodeName, err)
+	}
+
+	return groupPodsByWorkload(podList.Items), nil
```

```diff
+
+func groupPodsByWorkload(pods []corev1.Pod) map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod {
+	nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload := make(map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod)
+	for i := range pods {
+		pod := &pods[i]
+		wlName := coreindexer.IndexPodWorkloadSliceName(pod)
+		if len(wlName) > 0 {
+			key := types.NamespacedName{Name: wlName[0], Namespace: pod.Namespace}
+			nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload[key] = append(nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload[key], pod)
+		}
+	}
+	return nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload
+}

-// listPodsForWorkload returns pods belonging to a workload.

+func (r *nodeReconciler) checkPodsOnNode(ctx context.Context, nodeName string, wl *kueue.Workload, hasUntoleratedTaints bool, hasTASAssignment bool, nodeSelectorAssignedPods []*corev1.Pod) (workloadHealthCheck, error) {
+	podsToTerminate, hasProgressingPods, err := r.getPodsToTerminate(ctx, wl, nodeName, nodeSelectorAssignedPods)
+	if err != nil {
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthUnknown}, fmt.Errorf("failed to get pods to terminate for node %s: %w", nodeName, err)
+	}
+
+	if !hasTASAssignment {
+		// This node is not part of the workload's topology assignment. If pods are assigned
+		// here (e.g., late pods with old node selectors), they are stray and must be terminated.
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadHealthy, podsToTerminate: podsToTerminate}, nil
+	}
+
+	if hasProgressingPods && (!hasUntoleratedTaints || features.Enabled(features.TASReplaceNodeOnPodTermination)) {
+		return workloadHealthCheck{status: workloadToBeObserved, podsToTerminate: podsToTerminate}, nil
```

  I think using `workloadToBeObserved` might be problematic and unnecessary here. This code path will be used for "healthy" scenarios when taints exist, note that taints are used for all healthy gpu and tpu nodes, so this effectively means monitoring all such nodes in the cluster continously every 1s.
  
  I think this was more of a hack prior to introduction of the podHandler, and now we should be able to just react to pod transitions.
  
  Let me know if you encounter some complications here

```diff
@@ -125,33 +146,53 @@ func (r *nodeReconciler) Reconcile(ctx context.Context, req ctrl.Request) (ctrl.
 	}
 	nodeExists := err == nil

+	}
+
+	var timerExpired bool
+	if readyCondition != nil && readyCondition.Status != corev1.ConditionTrue {
+		timeSinceNotReady := r.clock.Now().Sub(readyCondition.LastTransitionTime.Time)
+		if timeSinceNotReady >= NodeFailureDelay {
+			timerExpired = true
+		} else if !features.Enabled(features.TASReplaceNodeOnPodTermination) {
+			return ctrl.Result{RequeueAfter: NodeFailureDelay - timeSinceNotReady}, nil
+		}
+	}
+
+	nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload, err := r.listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector(ctx, req.Name)
+	if err != nil {
+		return ctrl.Result{}, err
+	}

 	}

+		_, err := r.handleUnhealthyNode(ctx, req.Name, affectedWorkloads)

+	if timerExpired {

+		evictedWorkloads, err := r.handleUnhealthyNode(ctx, req.Name, affectedWorkloads)
+		if err != nil {
+			return ctrl.Result{}, err
+		}
+		// Only reconcile workloads that were not evicted.
+		affectedWorkloads = affectedWorkloads.Difference(evictedWorkloads)
```

  I think there might be a subtle race condition here in case there is a follow up Reconciel (to the reconcile which decided to evict a workload), and the  follow up Reconcile does not yet see the workload is evicted then it may take a decision to terminate the Pods. I'm not totally sure this would happen, but if this is the worst case scenario then I'm fine with it.

```diff
+// / listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector returns a map of pods that are assigned to this node via nodeSelector, grouped by workload.
+func (r *nodeReconciler) listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector(ctx context.Context, nodeName string) (map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod, error) {

+	if err := r.client.List(ctx, &podList, client.MatchingFields{indexer.PodNodeSelectorHostnameKey: nodeName}); err != nil {
+		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to list pods for node selector %s: %w", nodeName, err)
```

```diff
+// / listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector returns a map of pods that are assigned to this node via nodeSelector, grouped by workload.
+func (r *nodeReconciler) listPodsAssignedByNodeSelector(ctx context.Context, nodeName string) (map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod, error) {
+	var podList corev1.PodList
+	if err := r.client.List(ctx, &podList, client.MatchingFields{indexer.PodNodeSelectorHostnameKey: nodeName}); err != nil {
+		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to list pods for node selector %s: %w", nodeName, err)
+	}
+
+	return groupPodsByWorkload(podList.Items), nil

+
+func groupPodsByWorkload(pods []corev1.Pod) map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod {
+	nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload := make(map[types.NamespacedName][]*corev1.Pod)
+	for i := range pods {
+		pod := &pods[i]
+		wlName := coreindexer.IndexPodWorkloadSliceName(pod)
+		if len(wlName) > 0 {
+			key := types.NamespacedName{Name: wlName[0], Namespace: pod.Namespace}
+			nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload[key] = append(nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload[key], pod)
+		}
+	}
+	return nodeSelectorPodsByWorkload
```

```diff
+	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/controller/tas/indexer"
 	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/features"
+	utilclient "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/util/client"
 	utilpod "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/util/pod"
 	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/util/roletracker"
 	utiltas "sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/util/tas"
 	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/workload"
 	"sigs.k8s.io/kueue/pkg/workloadslicing"
 )
 
-type workloadStatus int
-
 const (
 	nodeMultipleFailuresEvictionMessageFormat = "Workload eviction triggered due to multiple TAS assigned node failures, including: %s"
 	podTerminationCheckPeriod                 = 1 * time.Second
```

  question: do we still need it? It does not seem used

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-03-18T08:33:20Z

- **pkg/controller/tas/node_controller.go:712** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-03-18T08:33:20Z
```diff
@@ -553,3 +674,51 @@ func classifyNoExecuteTaints(ctx context.Context, taints []corev1.Taint, podSets
 	}
 	return untolerated, temporarilyTolerated
 }
+
+var _ handler.EventHandler = (*nodeFailurePodHandler)(nil)
+
+type nodeFailurePodHandler struct {
+	client client.Client
+}
+
+func (h *nodeFailurePodHandler) Create(_ context.Context, e event.CreateEvent, q workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface[reconcile.Request]) {
+	h.queueReconcileForPod(e.Object, q)
+}
+
+func (h *nodeFailurePodHandler) Update(_ context.Context, e event.UpdateEvent, q workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface[reconcile.Request]) {
+	h.queueReconcileForPod(e.ObjectNew, q)
+}
+
+func (h *nodeFailurePodHandler) Delete(_ context.Context, e event.DeleteEvent, q workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface[reconcile.Request]) {
+	h.queueReconcileForPod(e.Object, q)
+}
+
+func (h *nodeFailurePodHandler) Generic(_ context.Context, _ event.GenericEvent, _ workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface[reconcile.Request]) {
+}
+
+func (h *nodeFailurePodHandler) queueReconcileForPod(object client.Object, q workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface[reconcile.Request]) {
+	pod, isPod := object.(*corev1.Pod)
+	if !isPod || !utiltas.IsTAS(pod) {
+		return
+	}
+
+	// queue for potential stuck pending pods
+	if len(pod.Spec.NodeName) == 0 && pod.Spec.NodeSelector != nil && len(pod.Spec.NodeSelector[corev1.LabelHostname]) > 0 {
+		req := reconcile.Request{
+			NamespacedName: types.NamespacedName{
+				Name: pod.Spec.NodeSelector[corev1.LabelHostname],
+			},
+		}
+		q.AddRateLimited(req)
```

  I would rather batch the reconciles. Previously we observed with 1s delay anyway, so I propose to introduce a const `reconcileBatchPeriod` and use it for `q.AddAfter`.

  Yes, batching in time, by key. When there are multiple events calling AddAfter within 1s (for the same key), they will trigger only one reconcile, the nearest one.


  this is description of the interface 
  
  ```go
  // TypedDelayingInterface is an Interface that can Add an item at a later time. This makes it easier to
  // requeue items after failures without ending up in a hot-loop.
  type TypedDelayingInterface[T comparable] interface {
  	TypedInterface[T]
  	// AddAfter adds an item to the workqueue after the indicated duration has passed
  	AddAfter(item T, duration time.Duration)
  }
  ```
  
  I think it just adds some delay
